<p><b>Regensburg</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[Àà ÅeÀê…°≈ãÃçsb ä…êÃØk]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Regensburg.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/De-Regensburg.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Regensburg.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>Castra-Regina</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <span lang="cs" xml:lang="cs"><i>≈òezno</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><i>Ratisbonne</i></span>; older English: <i>Ratisbon</i>) is a city in south-east <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, situated at the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naab" title="Naab">Naab</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regen_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Regen River">Regen</a> rivers. With over 140,000 inhabitants, Regensburg is the fourth-largest city in the State of <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> after <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a>. The city is the <a href="/wiki/Political" class="mw-redirect" title="Political">political</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic">economic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cultural" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural">cultural</a> centre of Eastern <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> and the capital of the Bavarian <a href="/wiki/Regierungsbezirk" title="Regierungsbezirk">administrative region</a> <a href="/wiki/Upper_Palatinate" title="Upper Palatinate">Upper Palatinate</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> centre of the city is a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> and a testimony of the city's status as cultural centre of southern Germany in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. In 2014, Regensburg was among the <a href="/wiki/Sightseeing" class="mw-redirect" title="Sightseeing">top sights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Germany" title="Tourism in Germany">travel attractions</a> in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-germany.travel_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-germany.travel-2">[2]</a></sup> Generally known in English as Ratisbon until well into the twentieth century, the city is known as Ratisbonne in French and as Ratisbona in Spanish, Italian, Portuguese, Catalan and Albanian.</p>
<p></p>

<ul>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg-porta-praetoria_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Regensburg-porta-praetoria_2.jpg/150px-Regensburg-porta-praetoria_2.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Regensburg-porta-praetoria_2.jpg/225px-Regensburg-porta-praetoria_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Regensburg-porta-praetoria_2.jpg/300px-Regensburg-porta-praetoria_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg-porta-praetoria_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The remains of the East Tower of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Porta_Praetoria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Porta Praetoria (page does not exist)">Porta Praetoria</a> of Roman times</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first settlements in Regensburg date from the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a> name <b>Radasbona</b> was the oldest given to a settlement near the present city. Around AD 90, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> built a fort there.</p>
<p>In 179, a new Roman fort <b>Castra Regina</b> ("fortress by the river Regen") was built for <a href="/wiki/Legio_III_Italica" title="Legio III Italica">Legio III <i>Italica</i></a> during the reign of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius" title="Marcus Aurelius">Marcus Aurelius</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BeerAdvocate_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeerAdvocate-3">[3]</a></sup> It was an important camp on the most northerly point of the Danube: it corresponds to what is today the core of Regensburg's Old City or <i>Altstadt</i> east of the Obere and Untere Bachgasse and West of the Schwanenplatz. It is believed that as early as in late Roman times the city was the seat of a bishop, and <a href="/wiki/St_Boniface" class="mw-redirect" title="St Boniface">St Boniface</a> re-established the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Regensburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Regensburg">Bishopric of Regensburg</a> in 739.</p>
<p>From the early 6th century, Regensburg was the seat of a ruling family known as the <a href="/wiki/Agilolfings" title="Agilolfings">Agilolfings</a>. From about 530 to the first half of the 13th century, it was the capital of Bavaria. Regensburg remained an important city during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>. In 792, Regensburg hosted the ecclesiastical section of Charlemagne's General Assembly, the <a href="/wiki/Bishops" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishops">bishops</a> in council who condemned the heresy of <a href="/wiki/Adoptionism" title="Adoptionism">adoptionism</a> taught by their Spanish counterparts, <a href="/wiki/Elipandus" class="mw-redirect" title="Elipandus">Elipandus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Felix_of_Urgel" class="mw-redirect" title="Felix of Urgel">Felix of Urgel</a>. After the partition of the Carolingian Empire in 843, the city became the seat of the Eastern <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> ruler, <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_German" title="Louis the German">Louis II</a> the German. Two years later, fourteen <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemian</a> princes came to Regensburg to receive <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptism</a> there. This was the starting point of <a href="/wiki/Christianization" title="Christianization">Christianization</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czechs</a>, and the diocese of Regensburg became the mother diocese of that of <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>. These events had a wide impact on the cultural history of the Czech lands, as they were consequently part of the Roman Catholic and not the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church#Conversion_of_East_and_South_Slavs" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Slavic-Orthodox world</a>. A memorial plate at St John's Church (the alleged place of the baptism) was unveiled a few years ago, commemorating the incident in the <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> languages.</p>
<p>On 8 December 899 <a href="/wiki/Arnulf_of_Carinthia" title="Arnulf of Carinthia">Arnulf of Carinthia</a>, descendant of <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>, died at Regensburg (known as Ratisbon at the time), <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 800&#160;AD the city had 23,000 inhabitants and by 1000&#160;AD this had almost doubled to 40,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-google_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1096, on the way to the <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">First Crusade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Hermit" title="Peter the Hermit">Peter the Hermit</a> led a mob of <a href="/wiki/Crusaders" class="mw-redirect" title="Crusaders">Crusaders</a> that attempted to force the mass conversion of the <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> of Regensburg and killed all those who resisted.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Braun_Regensburg_UBHD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Braun_Regensburg_UBHD.jpg/220px-Braun_Regensburg_UBHD.jpg" width="220" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Braun_Regensburg_UBHD.jpg/330px-Braun_Regensburg_UBHD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Braun_Regensburg_UBHD.jpg/440px-Braun_Regensburg_UBHD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1003" data-file-height="455" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Braun_Regensburg_UBHD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Regensburg in the 16th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 1135 and 1146, the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bridge_(Regensburg)" title="Stone Bridge (Regensburg)">Stone Bridge</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> was built at Regensburg. This bridge opened major international trade routes between northern Europe and <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, and this began Regensburg's golden age as a residence of wealthy trading families. Regensburg became the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Germany" title="Culture of Germany">cultural</a> centre of southern Germany and was celebrated for its gold work and fabrics.</p>

<tr>
<td colspan="3"><small>a: The <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Regensburg" title="Bishopric of Regensburg">Bishopric of Regensburg</a> acquired <a href="/wiki/Imperial_immediacy" title="Imperial immediacy">Imperial immediacy</a> around the same time as the City. Of the three <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Abbey" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Abbey">Imperial Abbeys</a> in Regensburg, <a href="/wiki/Niederm%C3%BCnster,_Regensburg" title="Niederm√ºnster, Regensburg">Niederm√ºnster</a> had already acquired immediacy in 1002, <a href="/wiki/St._Emmeram%27s_Abbey" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Emmeram's Abbey">St. Emmeram's Abbey</a> did in 1295 and <a href="/wiki/Oberm%C3%BCnster,_Regensburg" title="Oberm√ºnster, Regensburg">Oberm√ºnster</a> in 1315.<br />
b: The <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Regensburg" title="Bishopric of Regensburg">Bishopric</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">Imperial City</a> and all three Imperial Abbeys were <a href="/wiki/German_Mediatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="German Mediatisation">mediatised</a> simultaneously.</small></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In 1245 Regensburg became a <a href="/wiki/Free_Imperial_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Imperial City">Free Imperial City</a> and was a trade centre before the shifting of <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> in the late Middle Ages. At the end of the 15th century in 1486, Regensburg became part of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">Duchy of Bavaria</a>, but its independence was restored by the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> ten years later. The city adopted the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> in 1542 and its Town Council remained entirely <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a>. From 1663 to 1806, the city was the permanent seat of the Imperial Diet of the Holy Roman Empire, which became known as the <a href="/wiki/Perpetual_Diet_of_Regensburg" title="Perpetual Diet of Regensburg">Perpetual Diet of Regensburg</a>. Thus, Regensburg was one of the central towns of the Empire, attracting visitors in large numbers.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg_Reichstag_1711.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Regensburg_Reichstag_1711.jpg/220px-Regensburg_Reichstag_1711.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Regensburg_Reichstag_1711.jpg/330px-Regensburg_Reichstag_1711.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Regensburg_Reichstag_1711.jpg/440px-Regensburg_Reichstag_1711.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1096" data-file-height="704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg_Reichstag_1711.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ceremonial arrival at the Imperial Diet, 1711</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A minority of the population remained <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a>, and Roman Catholics were denied civil rights (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">B√ºrgerrecht</span></i>). But the town of Regensburg must not be confused with the Bishopric of Regensburg. Although the Imperial city had adopted the Reformation, the town remained the seat of a Roman Catholic bishop and several <a href="/wiki/Abbey" title="Abbey">abbeys</a>. Three of the latter, <a href="/wiki/St._Emmeram" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Emmeram">St. Emmeram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niederm%C3%BCnster" class="mw-redirect" title="Niederm√ºnster">Niederm√ºnster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oberm%C3%BCnster" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberm√ºnster">Oberm√ºnster</a>, were estates of their own within the Holy Roman Empire, meaning that they were granted a seat and a vote at the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Diet_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" title="Imperial Diet (Holy Roman Empire)">Imperial Diet</a> (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Reichstag</span></i>). So there was the unique situation that the town of Regensburg comprised five independent "states" (in terms of the Holy Roman Empire): the Protestant city itself, the Roman Catholic bishopric, and the three <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monasteries</a> (mentioned previously). In addition, it was seen as the traditional capital of the region Bavaria (not the state), acted as functional co-capital of the Empire (second to the Emperor's court at Vienna) due to the presence of the Perpetual Diet, and it was residence of the Emperor's Commissary-Principal to the same diet, who with one very brief exception was a prince himself (longstandingly the Prince <a href="/wiki/Thurn_and_Taxis" class="mw-redirect" title="Thurn and Taxis">Thurn and Taxis</a>, still resident in the town).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1803 the city lost its status as a free city, following its incorporation into the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Regensburg" title="Principality of Regensburg">Principality of Regensburg</a>. It was handed over to the <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishopric of Mainz">Archbishop of Mainz</a> and Archchancellor of the Holy Roman Empire <a href="/wiki/Carl_von_Dalberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Carl von Dalberg">Carl von Dalberg</a> in compensation for Mainz, which had become <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lun%C3%A9ville" title="Treaty of Lun√©ville">Treaty of Lun√©ville</a> in 1801. The archbishopric of Mainz was formally transferred to Regensburg. Dalberg united the bishopric, the monasteries, and the town itself, making up the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Regensburg" title="Principality of Regensburg">Principality of Regensburg</a> (<i>F√ºrstentum Regensburg</i>). Dalberg strictly modernized public life. Most importantly, he awarded equal rights to Protestants and Roman Catholics alike. In 1810 Dalberg ceded Regensburg to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">Kingdom of Bavaria</a>, he himself being compensated by the award of <a href="/wiki/Fulda" title="Fulda">Fulda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hanau" title="Hanau">Hanau</a> to him under the title of "<a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Frankfurt" title="Grand Duchy of Frankfurt">Grand Duke of Frankfurt</a>".</p>
<p>Between April 19 and April 23, 1809, Regensburg was the scene of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ratisbon" title="Battle of Ratisbon">Battle of Ratisbon</a> between forces commanded by <a href="/wiki/Henri_Gatien_Bertrand" title="Henri Gatien Bertrand">Henri Gatien Bertrand</a> and Napoleon himself and the retreating <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian</a> forces. The city was eventually overrun, after supplies and <a href="/wiki/Ammunition" title="Ammunition">ammunition</a> ran out. The city suffered severe damage during the fight, with about 150 houses being burnt and others being looted.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nazism_and_World_War_II">Nazism and World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nazism and World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regensburg was home to both a <a href="/wiki/Bf_109" class="mw-redirect" title="Bf 109">Messerschmitt Bf 109</a> aircraft factory and an oil refinery, which were bombed by the Allies on August 17, 1943, by the <a href="/wiki/Schweinfurt-Regensburg_mission" class="mw-redirect" title="Schweinfurt-Regensburg mission">Schweinfurt-Regensburg mission</a>, and on February 5, 1945, during the <a href="/wiki/Oil_Campaign_of_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil Campaign of World War II">Oil Campaign of World War II</a>. Although both targets were badly damaged, Regensburg itself suffered little damage from the Allied <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II" title="Strategic bombing during World War II">strategic bombing campaign</a>, and the nearly intact medieval city centre is listed as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>. The city's most important cultural loss was that of the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> church of <a href="/wiki/Oberm%C3%BCnster" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberm√ºnster">Oberm√ºnster</a>, which was destroyed in a March 1945 air raid and was not rebuilt (the <a href="/wiki/Bell_tower" title="Bell tower">belfry</a> survived). Also, Regensburg's slow economic recovery after the war ensured that historic buildings were not torn down, to be replaced by newer ones. When the upswing in restoration reached Regensburg in the late 1960s, the prevailing mindset had turned in favour of preserving the city's heritage.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_after_1945">History after 1945</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History after 1945">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:137px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ukrainian_Camp_Post_-_Regensburg_postmark.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ukrainian_Camp_Post_-_Regensburg_postmark.png/135px-Ukrainian_Camp_Post_-_Regensburg_postmark.png" width="135" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ukrainian_Camp_Post_-_Regensburg_postmark.png/203px-Ukrainian_Camp_Post_-_Regensburg_postmark.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ukrainian_Camp_Post_-_Regensburg_postmark.png/270px-Ukrainian_Camp_Post_-_Regensburg_postmark.png 2x" data-file-width="626" data-file-height="636" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ukrainian_Camp_Post_-_Regensburg_postmark.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cancellation_(mail)" title="Cancellation (mail)">Cancel</a> by the Ukrainian Camp Post at Regensburg DP Camp</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 1945 and 1949, Regensburg was the site of the largest <a href="/wiki/Displaced_persons_camp" title="Displaced persons camp">Displaced persons (DP) camp</a> in Germany. At its peak in 1946‚Äì1947, the workers' district of Ganghofersiedlung housed almost 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainian</a> and 1,000 non-Ukrainian refugees and displaced persons. With the approval of U.S. Military Government in the American <a href="/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany" title="Allied-occupied Germany">Allied Occupation Zone</a>, Regensburg and other DP camps organised their own camp postal service. In Regensburg, the camp postal service began operation on December 11, 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of the 1960s, Regensburg invested a lot in technical and social <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> to attract industry. <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> was the first multinational company to come to Regensburg, a milestone in the city's development after World War II. In 1965, <a href="/wiki/Regensburg_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Regensburg University">Regensburg University</a> was founded, <a href="/wiki/Regensburg_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Regensburg University of Applied Sciences">Regensburg University of Applied Sciences</a> was established in 1971. The second multinational company, <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, came in 1986 to build up a large production plant. Since the 1990s, several well-known <a href="/wiki/Hightech" class="mw-redirect" title="Hightech">hightech</a> companies are located in Regensburg, such as Infineon and OSRAM, contributing to the city's current wealth.</p>
<p>In 1997, Regensburg was awarded the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Europe_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Europe Prize (page does not exist)">Europe Prize</a> for its outstanding achievements in <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">european integration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-europeprize_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europeprize-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Committee" title="World Heritage Committee">World Heritage Committee</a> listed Regensburg's Old Town a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> in July 2006. It is the largest medieval old town north of the Alps and very well preserved, dubbing it "Italy's most northern city". Close to the Stone Bridge, the city of Regensburg established a World Heritage Centre in the historic Salzstadl in 2007, where detailed information on Regensburg's 2000-year-old history is given.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regensburg is situated on the northernmost part of the Danube river at the geological crossroads of four distinct <a href="/wiki/Landscape" title="Landscape">landscapes</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li>to the north and northeast lies the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Forest" title="Bavarian Forest">Bavarian Forest</a> (Bayerischer Wald) with <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gneiss" title="Gneiss">gneiss</a> mountains, wide forests and its <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Forest_National_Park" title="Bavarian Forest National Park">national park</a></li>
<li>to the east and south-east is the fertile Danube plain (G√§uboden) which are highly cultivated <a href="/wiki/Loess" title="Loess">loess</a> plains</li>
<li>the south is dominated by the tertiary hill country (Terti√§r-H√ºgelland), a continuation of <a href="/wiki/Alpine_foothills" title="Alpine foothills">Alpine foothills</a></li>
<li>to the West is <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Jura" title="Franconian Jura">Franconian Jura</a> (Fr√§nkische Jura)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> in Regensburg is categorized in the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K√∂ppen climate classification">K√∂ppen climate classification</a> as Dfb (<a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental</a>). The average temperature of 8.5&#160;¬∞C (47.3&#160;¬∞F) is slightly above the German average (7.8&#160;¬∞C or 46.0&#160;¬∞F), the average precipitation of 636 millimetres (25.0 <a href="/wiki/Inch" title="Inch">inches</a>) per year below the German average (approximately 700 millimetres or 28 inches ). With a total of 1670 sunshine hours per year, Regensburg is roughly 120 hours above German average.<sup id="cite_ref-uni-regensburg_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni-regensburg-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The warmest month of the year, on average, is July. The coolest month of the year, on average, is January.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_city">The city</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The city">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg_cathedral_front.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Regensburg_cathedral_front.jpg/200px-Regensburg_cathedral_front.jpg" width="200" height="366" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Regensburg_cathedral_front.jpg/300px-Regensburg_cathedral_front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Regensburg_cathedral_front.jpg/400px-Regensburg_cathedral_front.jpg 2x" data-file-width="718" data-file-height="1315" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg_square.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Regensburg_square.jpg/200px-Regensburg_square.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Regensburg_square.jpg/300px-Regensburg_square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Regensburg_square.jpg/400px-Regensburg_square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>

Kohlenmarkt with Town Hall, site of the <a href="/wiki/Perpetual_Diet_of_Regensburg" title="Perpetual Diet of Regensburg">Perpetual Diet</a> from 1663 to 1806.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SchlossThurnundTaxis2010.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/SchlossThurnundTaxis2010.JPG/200px-SchlossThurnundTaxis2010.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/SchlossThurnundTaxis2010.JPG/300px-SchlossThurnundTaxis2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/SchlossThurnundTaxis2010.JPG/400px-SchlossThurnundTaxis2010.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SchlossThurnundTaxis2010.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/St._Emmeram%27s_Abbey" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Emmeram's Abbey">St. Emmeram's Abbey</a>, now Schloss <a href="/wiki/Thurn_und_Taxis" title="Thurn und Taxis">Thurn und Taxis</a>, a huge palace</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Regensburg includes the largest medieval old town north of the Alps with nearly 1,500 <a href="/wiki/Listed_buildings" class="mw-redirect" title="Listed buildings">listed buildings</a> and a picturesque <a href="/wiki/Cityscape" title="Cityscape">cityscape</a>. Its most famous sights are located mainly in the Old Town, such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Regensburg_Cathedral" title="Regensburg Cathedral">Dom</a></i> (Cathedral) is an example of pure German <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> and counts as the main work of Gothic architecture in Bavaria. It was founded in 1275 and completed in 1634, with the exception of the towers, which were finished in 1869. The interior contains numerous interesting monuments, including one of <a href="/wiki/Peter_Vischer" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter Vischer">Peter Vischer</a>'s masterpieces. Adjoining the <a href="/wiki/Cloister" title="Cloister">cloisters</a> are two chapels of earlier date than the cathedral itself, one of which, known as the old cathedral, goes back perhaps to the 8th century. The official choir for the liturgical music at St Peter's Cathedral are the famous <a href="/wiki/Regensburger_Domspatzen" title="Regensburger Domspatzen">Regensburger Domspatzen</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bridge_(Regensburg)" title="Stone Bridge (Regensburg)">stone bridge</a>, built 1135‚Äì1146, is a highlight of medieval bridge building. The knights of the 2nd and 3rd <a href="/wiki/Crusade" class="mw-redirect" title="Crusade">crusade</a> used it to cross the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> on their way to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Regensburg_Sausage_Kitchen" title="Regensburg Sausage Kitchen">Regensburg Sausage Kitchen</a> is a major tourist destination, but locals eat there as well. It was originally built as the construction headquarters of the stone bridge and now lies adjacent to it.</li>
<li>Remains of the Roman fortress' walls including the Porta Praetoria</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Scots_Monastery,_Regensburg" title="Scots Monastery, Regensburg">Church of St. James</a>, also called <i>Schottenkirche</i>, a Romanesque basilica of the 12th century, derives its name from the monastery of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Irish</a> <a href="/wiki/Benedictine" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedictine">Benedictines</a> (<a href="/wiki/Scoti" title="Scoti">Scoti</a>) to which it was attached; the principal doorway is covered with very singular grotesque carvings. It stands next to the <i>Jakobstor</i>, a medieval city gate named after it.</li>
<li>The old parish church of <i><a href="/wiki/Ulrich_of_Zell" title="Ulrich of Zell">St. Ulrich</a></i> is a good example of the Transition style of the 13th century, and contains a valuable antiquarian collection. It houses the diocesan museum for religious art.</li>
<li>Examples of the Romanesque basilica style are the church of <i><a href="/wiki/Oberm%C3%BCnster" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberm√ºnster">Oberm√ºnster</a></i>, dating from 1010, and the abbey church of <i><a href="/wiki/St._Emmeram" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Emmeram">St. Emmeram</a></i>, built in the 13th century, remarkable as one of the few German churches with a detached bell tower. The beautiful cloisters of the ancient abbey, one of the oldest in Germany, are still in a fair state of preservation. In 1809 the conventual buildings were converted into a palace for the prince of <a href="/wiki/Thurn_und_Taxis" title="Thurn und Taxis">Thurn and Taxis</a>, hereditary postmaster-general of the Holy Roman Empire.</li>
<li>The Adler-Apotheke, located nearby the Regensburg Cathedral, was founded in 1610 and is one of the oldest Pharmacies in Regensburg. Even today you can take a look at the ancient interior and historical vessels.</li>
<li>Wealthy patrician families competed against each other to see who would be able to build the highest tower of the city. In 1260, the <i>Goldener Turm</i> (golden tower) was built on Wahlenstra√üe.</li>
<li>The Old Town Hall, dating in part from the 14th century, contains the rooms occupied by the Imperial diet from 1663 to 1806.</li>
<li>A historical interest is also attached to the <i>Gasthof zum Goldenen Kreuz</i> (Golden Cross Inn), where <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> made the acquaintance of Barbara Blomberg, the mother of <a href="/wiki/Don_John_of_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Don John of Austria">Don John of Austria</a> (born 1547).</li>
<li>Perhaps the most pleasant modern building in the city is the Gothic villa of the king of Bavaria on the bank of the Danube.</li>
<li>Among the public institutions of the city are the public <a href="/wiki/Library" title="Library">library</a>, picture gallery, <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a>, and the institute for the making of <a href="/wiki/Stained_glass" title="Stained glass">stained glass</a>. The city's colleges (apart from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Regensburg" title="University of Regensburg">University of Regensburg</a>) include an <a href="/wiki/Bishop" title="Bishop">episcopal</a> clerical <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a>, and a school of <a href="/wiki/Religious_music" title="Religious music">church music</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._Emmeram%27s_Abbey" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Emmeram's Abbey">St. Emmeram's Abbey</a>, now known as Schloss Thurn und Taxis, is a huge castle owned by the powerful Thurn and Taxis family.</li>
<li>The City Park, the oldest and largest park in Regensburg with a lot of artwork</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_der_Universit%C3%A4t_Regensburg" title="Botanischer Garten der Universit√§t Regensburg">Botanischer Garten der Universit√§t Regensburg</a> is a modern <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a> located on the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Regensburg" title="University of Regensburg">University of Regensburg</a> campus.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Herzogspark" title="Herzogspark">Herzogspark</a> also contains several small botanical gardens.</li>
</ul>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg_Uferpanorama_06_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Regensburg_Uferpanorama_06_2006.jpg/800px-Regensburg_Uferpanorama_06_2006.jpg" width="800" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Regensburg_Uferpanorama_06_2006.jpg/1200px-Regensburg_Uferpanorama_06_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Regensburg_Uferpanorama_06_2006.jpg/1600px-Regensburg_Uferpanorama_06_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5249" data-file-height="1000" /></a>

</div>
</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_surrounding">The surrounding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The surrounding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walhalla_aussen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Walhalla_aussen.jpg/150px-Walhalla_aussen.jpg" width="150" height="98" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Walhalla_aussen.jpg/225px-Walhalla_aussen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Walhalla_aussen.jpg/300px-Walhalla_aussen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="625" data-file-height="410" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walhalla_aussen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Klenze's <a href="/wiki/Walhalla_temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Walhalla temple"><i>Walhalla</i></a>, built in 1842</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Postwertzeichen_DPAG_-_Bayerischer_Wald_2005_hi_res_scan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Postwertzeichen_DPAG_-_Bayerischer_Wald_2005_hi_res_scan.jpg/150px-Postwertzeichen_DPAG_-_Bayerischer_Wald_2005_hi_res_scan.jpg" width="150" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Postwertzeichen_DPAG_-_Bayerischer_Wald_2005_hi_res_scan.jpg/225px-Postwertzeichen_DPAG_-_Bayerischer_Wald_2005_hi_res_scan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Postwertzeichen_DPAG_-_Bayerischer_Wald_2005_hi_res_scan.jpg/300px-Postwertzeichen_DPAG_-_Bayerischer_Wald_2005_hi_res_scan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="848" data-file-height="856" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Postwertzeichen_DPAG_-_Bayerischer_Wald_2005_hi_res_scan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bavarian Forest National Park stamp</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Near Regensburg there are two very imposing <a href="/wiki/Classicism" title="Classicism">Classical buildings</a>, erected by <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_I_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig I of Bavaria">Ludwig I of Bavaria</a> as national monuments to German patriotism and greatness:</p>
<ul>
<li>The more imposing of the two is the <i><a href="/wiki/Walhalla_temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Walhalla temple">Walhalla</a></i>, a costly reproduction of the <a href="/wiki/Parthenon" title="Parthenon">Parthenon</a>, erected as a <a href="/wiki/Teutons" title="Teutons">Teutonic</a> temple of fame on a hill rising from the Danube at <a href="/wiki/Donaustauf" title="Donaustauf">Donaustauf</a>, 10 kilometres (6.2 miles) to the east. The interior, which is as rich as coloured <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilding" title="Gilding">gilding</a>, and sculptures can make it, contains the <a href="/wiki/Bust_(sculpture)" title="Bust (sculpture)">busts</a> of more than a hundred Germanic worthies</li>
<li>The second of King Ludwig's buildings is the <i><a href="/wiki/Befreiungshalle" title="Befreiungshalle">Befreiungshalle</a></i> at <a href="/wiki/Kelheim" title="Kelheim">Kelheim</a>, 25 kilometres (16 miles) above Regensburg, a large circular building which has for its aim the glorification of the heroes of the 1813 <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">War of Liberation</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Besides, there is the famous <a href="/wiki/Weltenburg_Abbey" title="Weltenburg Abbey">Weltenburg Abbey</a> (Kloster Weltenburg), a Benedictine monastery in Weltenburg near Kelheim on the Danube. The abbey is situated on a peninsula in the Danube, on the so-called "Weltenburg Narrows" or the "Danube Gorge". The monastery, founded by Irish or Scottish monks in about 620, is held to be the oldest monastery in Bavaria.</p>
<p>To the east of Regensburg lies the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Forest" title="Bavarian Forest">Bavarian Forest</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Forest_National_Park" title="Bavarian Forest National Park">National Park</a>, one of the most visited <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected areas</a> in Germany.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_exhibitions">Museums and exhibitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Museums and exhibitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Altogether Regensburg is home to 20 museums. Among the most prominent museums are for instance the <a href="/wiki/Regensburg_Museum_of_History" title="Regensburg Museum of History">Regensburg Museum of History</a> which shows history, culture and arts of Regensburg and Eastern Bavaria from <a href="/wiki/Stone_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Stone age">stone age</a> to present. Then there is the Imperial diet museum (Reichstagsmuseum) in the Old Town Hall describing the life during the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. Its main attractions are an original torture chamber and the Reichssaal, the rooms occupied by the Imperial diet from 1663 to 1806. The Kepler Memorial House (Keplerged√§chtnishaus) illustrates the life of the famous astronomer and mathematician <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Johannes Kepler</a>. The Municipal <a href="/wiki/Art_Gallery" class="mw-redirect" title="Art Gallery">Art Gallery</a> <i>Leerer Beutel</i> offers art collections, film events and cultural festivals. Over the last years, the city added several outdoor museums to its cultural landscape, the so-called <i>document</i> sites. These give an overview on specific topics such as <a href="/wiki/Roman_History" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman History">Roman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jewish_history" title="Jewish history">Jewish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Bavarian history">Bavarian history</a>.</p>
<p>Besides, there are the <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">diocese</a> museums (Bistumsmuseen) of Regensburg and a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_National_Museum" title="Bavarian National Museum">Bavarian National Museum</a> located in the St. Emmeram's Abbey, which contains the Princely Treasure Chamber of the family <a href="/wiki/Thurn_and_Taxis" class="mw-redirect" title="Thurn and Taxis">Thurn and Taxis</a>. The Domschatzmuseum where church treasures, monstrances and tapestries are displayed is in <a href="/wiki/Regensburg_Cathedral" title="Regensburg Cathedral">St. Peter's Cathedral</a>. Other museums are the Kunstforum Ostdeutsche Galerie, the Naturkundemuseum Ostbayern, the <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptile</a> zoo, the <a href="/wiki/Regensburg_Museum_of_Danube_Shipping" title="Regensburg Museum of Danube Shipping">Regensburg Museum of Danube Shipping</a> (Donau-Schiffahrts-Museum), the Public Observatory Regensburg as well as the watch museum (Uhrenmuseum), the golf museum, the post museum and the Dinoraeum. To celebrate its centenary, the State of Bavaria will open the museum of Bavarian history in Regensburg in May, 2018. Besides, there are guided tours in most of the historical monuments of Regensburg, as well as organized tourist tours through the city available in several languages.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theaters">Theaters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Theaters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg_Stadttheater_Zuschauerraum_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Regensburg_Stadttheater_Zuschauerraum_2004.jpg/150px-Regensburg_Stadttheater_Zuschauerraum_2004.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Regensburg_Stadttheater_Zuschauerraum_2004.jpg/225px-Regensburg_Stadttheater_Zuschauerraum_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Regensburg_Stadttheater_Zuschauerraum_2004.jpg/300px-Regensburg_Stadttheater_Zuschauerraum_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="384" data-file-height="512" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg_Stadttheater_Zuschauerraum_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Inside Regensburg Theater</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Regensburg Theater at the Bismarckplatz is 200 years old and is the most important theater of the city. Operas, operettas, musicals and ballets are shown. In summer, open-air performances are carried out as well. With the theater at the Bismarckplatz as the oldest and largest one, the Regensburg theater has four other stages with programmes that complement each other:<sup id="cite_ref-regensburgtravel_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regensburgtravel-12">[12]</a></sup> in the <i>Neuhaussaal</i> of the theater at the Bismarckplatz, concerts by the Philharmonic Orchestra Regensburg take place. The Velodrom Theater presents musicals and plays. In the Haidplatz Theater mainly literary and modern plays are performed, whereas the Turmtheater at the Goliathplatz shows modern plays as well, but also cabarets, musicals and plays for children.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regensburg is home to the famous <a href="/wiki/Regensburger_Domspatzen" title="Regensburger Domspatzen">Regensburger Domspatzen</a>. Since 2003 there are the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburger_Schlossfestspiele&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Regensburger Schlossfestspiele (page does not exist)">Regensburger Schlossfestspiele</a> in the inner courtyard of the <a href="/wiki/St._Emmeram%27s_Abbey" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Emmeram's Abbey">St. Emmeram's Abbey</a> every July, sponsored by the Princely Family of Thurn und Taxis. Meanwhile, those were attracting musicians like <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Garrett_(musician)" title="David Garrett (musician)">David Garrett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Jones_(singer)" title="Tom Jones (singer)">Tom Jones</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pl%C3%A1cido_Domingo" title="Pl√°cido Domingo">Pl√°cido Domingo</a>. Modern music styles, especially <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">Jazz</a>, are presented every summer during the Bavarian Jazz weekend. All over the Old Town, over hundred bands, combos and soloists are performing. In 2015, the House of Music was opened, giving home to skilled musicians and their education.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_cinema">Film and cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Film and cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The international <a href="/wiki/Short_film" title="Short film">short film</a> season is hosted annually in Regensburg. It is a non-profit event and takes place every March, being one of the most important of its type in Germany. Aside, there are several cinemas, such as CinemaxX, the largest one showing <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_(entertainment)" title="Blockbuster (entertainment)">blockbusters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthouse_film" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthouse film">arthouse films</a>, and smaller independent cinemas such as Garbo, Ostentor Kino and Regina Filmtheater. Regensburg has two <a href="/wiki/Open_air_cinemas" class="mw-redirect" title="Open air cinemas">open air cinemas</a> as well.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buildings">Buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Old Town of Regensburg with nearly 1,500 <a href="/wiki/Listed_buildings" class="mw-redirect" title="Listed buildings">listed buildings</a> offers a huge cultural diversity from Roman to modern times.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">Recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Old Town of Regensburg is surrounded completely by a <a href="/wiki/Green_belt" title="Green belt">green belt</a>. Numerous inner-city parks like the City Park (<i>Stadtpark</i>), the <i>Herzogspark</i>, the <i>D√∂rnbergpark</i>, the <i>Villapark</i> or the university's <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a> are a source for recreation and leisure.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorial_sites">Memorial sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Memorial sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city of Regensburg erected several memorials to combat <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_tolerance" class="mw-redirect" title="Social tolerance">intolerance</a> towards minorities and all other forms of contempt for <a href="/wiki/Human_dignity" class="mw-redirect" title="Human dignity">human dignity</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Memorial for the victims of the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a></li>
<li>Memorial for the victims of <a href="/wiki/Euthanasy" class="mw-redirect" title="Euthanasy">euthanasy</a></li>
<li>Memorial for <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp">concentration camp</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_prisoners" class="mw-redirect" title="War prisoners">war prisoners</a></li>
<li>Memorial for <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">violence against women</a></li>
</ul>
<p>A specific in Regensburg are the so-called <i>Stolpersteine</i> (stumbling blocks) in honor of deported Jews during <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Twice a year takes place the Regensburg Dult, the city's <a href="/wiki/Volksfest" title="Volksfest">Volksfest</a>, which is Bavaria's fourth largest. The B√ºrgerfest (citizen celebration) in the Old Town is every two years, attracting over 100,000 visitors. Every second weekend in July, knights and other medieval people come together at the Regensburg Spectaculum, a medieval market, on the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bridge_(Regensburg)" title="Stone Bridge (Regensburg)">Stone Bridge</a>. Every December, there are several <a href="/wiki/Christmas_markets" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas markets">Christmas markets</a> all over the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nightlife">Nightlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Nightlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With over 500 bars, restaurants, clubs and other locations merely in the inner city, Regensburg provides a rich and diverse <a href="/wiki/Nightlife" title="Nightlife">nightlife</a> due to its young population.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, Regensburg had 140,276 <a href="/wiki/Inhabitants" class="mw-redirect" title="Inhabitants">inhabitants</a>, making it the fourth largest city in Bavaria. Over the last hundred years, the city has experienced a strong increase in population, surpassing 100,000 inhabitants in 1945 due to Germans who were <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_(1944-1950)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans (1944-1950)">ethnically cleansed</a> from eastern parts of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a>, especially from the <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">Sudetenland</a>. Today, Regensburg is one of fastest growing cities in Germany and is supposed to reach 150,000 inhabitants in the near future.<br />
<a href="/wiki/File:Population_Statistics_Regensburg.svg" class="image" title="Regensburg's population since 1830"><img alt="Regensburg's population since 1830" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Population_Statistics_Regensburg.svg/300px-Population_Statistics_Regensburg.svg.png" width="300" height="180" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Population_Statistics_Regensburg.svg/450px-Population_Statistics_Regensburg.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Population_Statistics_Regensburg.svg/600px-Population_Statistics_Regensburg.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="450" /></a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_communities">International communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: International communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nearly 12% of the total population are foreign residents. Most of them come from <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><br /></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A majority of Regensburg's population is <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>. In 2013, about 56.5% of the city's inhabitants identified with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, 14.0% were registered <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> and about 29.5% identified with other religions or did not have any registered religious affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-regensburg_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regensburg-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor">Lord Mayor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/City_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="City Council">City Council</a> are elected for a period of six years. Both elections take place at the same time. The City Council is composed of 51 members and includes the Lord Mayor, two deputy mayors, five counsellors and the other council members.</p>

<p>After 18 years of a City Council with <a href="/wiki/Conservative" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative">conservative</a> majority, the <a href="/wiki/Social-democratic" class="mw-redirect" title="Social-democratic">social-democratic</a> candidate, Joachim Wolbergs, became Lord Mayor in Mai 2014.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boroughs">Boroughs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Boroughs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regensburg is subdivided into 18 <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">boroughs</a> (Stadtbezirke): Innenstadt, Stadtamhof, Steinweg-Pfaffenstein, Sallern-Gallingkofen, Konradsiedlung-Wutzlhofen, Brandlberg-Keilberg, Reinhausen, Weichs, Schwabelweis, Ostenviertel, Kasernenviertel, Galgenberg, Kumpfm√ºhl-Ziegetsdorf-Neupr√ºll, Gro√üpr√ºfening-Dechbetten-K√∂nigswiesen, Westenviertel, Ober- und Niederwinzer-Kager, Oberisling-Gra√ü, Burgweinting-Harting. Each borough contains a number of localities (Ortsteile), which can have historic roots in older municipalities that became urbanized and incorporated into the city.</p>
<h3><span id="Twin_towns_‚Äì_Sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_Sister_cities">Twin towns ‚Äì Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Twin towns ‚Äì Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regensburg is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr valign="top">
<td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Regensburg's economy counts among the most dynamic and fastest growing in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-prognos_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prognos-17">[17]</a></sup> Focus is on manufacturing industries, such as <a href="/wiki/Automotive" class="mw-redirect" title="Automotive">automotive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industrial_engineering" title="Industrial engineering">industrial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Companies">Companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are several <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporations</a> located in Regensburg, such as <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continental_AG" title="Continental AG">Continental</a>, <a href="/wiki/E.ON" title="E.ON">E.ON</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Infineon" class="mw-redirect" title="Infineon">Infineon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osram" title="Osram">Osram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schneider_Electric" title="Schneider Electric">Schneider Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Telekom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">Toshiba</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Hidden_champions" title="Hidden champions">hidden champions</a> (<a href="/wiki/Krones" title="Krones">Krones</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maschinenfabrik_Reinhausen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maschinenfabrik Reinhausen (page does not exist)">MR</a>).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a> operates an automobile production plant in Regensburg; the Regensburg BMW plant produces <a href="/wiki/BMW_3_Series" title="BMW 3 Series">3 Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMW_1_Series" title="BMW 1 Series">1 Series</a> and (previously) Z4 vehicles. <a href="/wiki/Continental_AG" title="Continental AG">Continental AG</a>, with the headquarters of its car component business, <a href="/wiki/Osram" title="Osram">Osram</a> Opto-Semiconductors and <a href="/wiki/Siemens_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Siemens AG">Siemens</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Infineon" class="mw-redirect" title="Infineon">Infineon</a>, the former Siemens semiconductor branch, provide a high level of <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a> and technical development in Regensburg. Other well known international companies, such as <a href="/wiki/AREVA" class="mw-redirect" title="AREVA">AREVA</a>, Schneider Electric and Toshiba, have built plants in or near Regensburg. <a href="/wiki/GE_Aviation" title="GE Aviation">GE Aviation</a> founded a greenfield site to innovate, develop and produce turbinemachinery components with a new manufacturing casting technology. <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a> located its first German customer service centre in Regensburg. The hidden champions <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maschinenfabrik_Reinhausen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maschinenfabrik Reinhausen (page does not exist)">Maschinenfabrik Reinhausen</a> (MR) and <a href="/wiki/Krones" title="Krones">Krones</a> both are headquartered in or close to Regensburg and are among the major employeurs.</p>
<p>Aside from the industrial sector, <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> contributes a lot to Regensburg's economical growth, especially since 2006, when the city gained status as <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage site">UNESCO World Heritage site</a>. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Regensburg" title="University of Regensburg">University of Regensburg</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Regensburg_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Regensburg University of Applied Sciences">Regensburg University of Applied Sciences</a> and mercantile trade also play major roles in Regensburg's economy. Increasingly, <a href="/wiki/Biotech" class="mw-redirect" title="Biotech">biotech</a> companies were founded in Regensburg over the last two decades and have their headquarters and laboratories in the city's "BioPark". Another focus is on <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>, with the city running a start-up centre for IT firms. One of these former start-ups, <a href="/wiki/CipSoft_GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="CipSoft GmbH">CipSoft GmbH</a>, now is a known video game company still based in Regensburg.</p>
<p>OTTI, the Eastern Bavaria Technology Transfer-Institut e.V., is headquartered in Regensburg.<sup id="cite_ref-otti_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otti-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city recorded 912,238 overnight hotel stays and 531,943 hotel guests in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-regensburg2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regensburg2-19">[19]</a></sup> Tourism figures have nearly doubled within the last 15 years and Regensburg has become one of the most-visited German cities from 100,000 to 500,000 residents. In 2014, Regensburg was ranked as a Top-30 travel attraction in Germany by international tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-germany.travel_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-germany.travel-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Regensburg_Hauptbahnhof" title="Regensburg Hauptbahnhof">Regensburg Hauptbahnhof</a> (central station) is connected to lines to <a href="/wiki/Munich%E2%80%93Regensburg_railway" title="Munich‚ÄìRegensburg railway">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg%E2%80%93Regensburg_railway" title="Nuremberg‚ÄìRegensburg railway">Nuremberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regensburg%E2%80%93Passau_railway" title="Regensburg‚ÄìPassau railway">Passau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regensburg%E2%80%93Hof_railway" title="Regensburg‚ÄìHof railway">Hof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danube_Valley_Railway_(Bavaria)" title="Danube Valley Railway (Bavaria)">Ingolstadt and Ulm</a>. The city lies also on two motorways, the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_3" title="Bundesautobahn 3">A3</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_93" title="Bundesautobahn 93">A93</a> from Holledau to <a href="/wiki/Hof,_Bavaria" title="Hof, Bavaria">Hof</a>.</p>
<p>The local transport is provided by a bus network run by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rvv.de/">RVV (Regensburger Verkehrsverbund)</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regensburg's energy is mainly supplied by the German company <a href="/wiki/E.ON" title="E.ON">E.ON</a>, one of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Electric_utility" title="Electric utility">electric utility</a> service providers. Its subsidiary Bayernwerk runs the local <a href="/wiki/Hydropower_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydropower station">hydropower station</a> in the Danube River. In 2012, about 9,1% of the total <a href="/wiki/Electricity_consumption" class="mw-redirect" title="Electricity consumption">electricity consumption</a> was generated by <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> sources, about 5,1% of the total heat consumption were generated by renewables.<sup id="cite_ref-regensburg3_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regensburg3-20">[20]</a></sup> Both figures show, that Regensburg is behind other Bavarian cities in this context. Therefore, the municipal government presented an energy plan in 2014, which should enhance the transformation towards renewable energy sources over the next decade.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regensburg hosts one of the most modern <a href="/wiki/University_hospitals" class="mw-redirect" title="University hospitals">university hospitals</a> in Europe, the <i>Universit√§tsklinikum Regensburg</i>. Aside, there are several other renowned hospitals such as the <i>Krankenhaus Barmherzige Br√ºder</i> and the <i>St. Josef-Krankenhaus</i>. In the <i>Bezirksklinikum</i>, mental diseases are treated. With 19,4 <a href="/wiki/Hospital_bed" title="Hospital bed">hospital beds</a> per 1000 residents, Regensburg owns the fourth highest density of beds per residents in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-destatis_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-destatis-21">[21]</a></sup> Concerning <a href="/wiki/Medical_doctor" class="mw-redirect" title="Medical doctor">medical doctors</a> per residents, Regensburg obtains the third place in Germany (339 per 100,000 residents).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city's BioPark, representing Bavaria's second largest <a href="/wiki/Biotech" class="mw-redirect" title="Biotech">biotech</a> cluster, hosts numerous <a href="/wiki/Research_institutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Research institutions">research institutions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biotech_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Biotech company">biotech companies</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities_and_academia">Universities and academia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Universities and academia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regensburg is known for its institutions of higher education. The biggest of those is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Regensburg" title="University of Regensburg">University of Regensburg</a>. Founded in 1962, it is one of Germany's youngest institutions and ranked among the Top 400 universities worldwide. Among the prominent thinkers associated with the institution are <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Udo_Steiner" title="Udo Steiner">Udo Steiner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Wiegard" title="Wolfgang Wiegard">Wolfgang Wiegard</a>. The campus is situated in one area together with the <a href="/wiki/Regensburg_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Regensburg University of Applied Sciences">Regensburg University of Applied Sciences</a>.</p>
<p>Since 1874 there has been a College of Catholic Music, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hochschule_f%C3%BCr_Katholische_Kirchenmusik_und_Musikp%C3%A4dagogik_Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hochschule f√ºr Katholische Kirchenmusik und Musikp√§dagogik Regensburg (page does not exist)">Hochschule f√ºr Katholische Kirchenmusik und Musikp√§dagogik Regensburg</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addtition to the research centres and institutes of the universities, there are several <a href="/wiki/Research_institutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Research institutions">research institutions</a> situated in the city of Regensburg. Among them are the Leibniz-Institute for East and Southeast European Studies (IOS), the Regensburg Centre for Interventional Immunology (RCI), the Fraunhofer Institute for Toxicology and Experimental Medicine (ITEM) and the BioPark, the Bavarian <a href="/wiki/Biotech" class="mw-redirect" title="Biotech">biotech</a> cluster.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regensburg is home to 18 <a href="/wiki/Elementary_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Elementary schools">elementary schools</a>. There are several institutions of <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary education</a>, both public and private, representing all levels of the German school system. There are eight Gymnasiums in Regensburg, five Realschule, six Hauptschule and four <a href="/wiki/Vocational_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Vocational schools">vocational schools</a> (the so-called Berufsschule). In addition, there are several folk high schools with different specialisations. Aside, there is the Swiss International School which is offering families an international educational infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/SSV_Jahn_Regensburg" title="SSV Jahn Regensburg">SSV Jahn Regensburg</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Germany" title="Football in Germany">local football club</a> and attracts a fairly large local following. The team was part of a larger sports club founded in 1889 as <i>Turnerbund Jahn Regensburg</i> which took its name from <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Ludwig_Jahn" title="Friedrich Ludwig Jahn">Friedrich Ludwig Jahn</a>, whose ideas of gymnastics greatly influenced German sport in the 19th century. The football department was created in 1907. The footballers and swimmers left their parent club in 1924 to form <i>Sportbund Jahn Regensburg</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ice_hockey">Ice hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Ice hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=EV_Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EV Regensburg (page does not exist)">EV Regensburg</a> is the local <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> club, currently playing in the <a href="/wiki/Oberliga_(ice_hockey)" title="Oberliga (ice hockey)">Oberliga S√ºd</a>, Germany's third highest professional league.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball">Baseball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Baseball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Buchbinder_Legion%C3%A4re_Regensburg" title="Buchbinder Legion√§re Regensburg">Regensburg Legion√§re</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a> club from Regensburg. The team is also known as Buchbinder Legion√§re, following a sponsorship of the Buchbinder company. The club is playing in the German <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(baseball)" title="Bundesliga (baseball)">Bundesliga</a> and is one of the most famous and most successful baseball clubs in Germany. Several players now playing in the <a href="/wiki/MLB" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB">MLB</a> formerly played at the club. Its arena, Armin-Wolf-Arena, was built in 1996 and has a capacity of 10,000 spectators, making it to Germany's largest <a href="/wiki/Baseball_stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball stadium">baseball stadium</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Regensburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The local <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a> club, LG TELIS FINANZ Regensburg, offers a wide range of different competitions and is counted among the most successful clubs in Germany.</p>
